   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Google Lunar X Prize
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       For the visual phenomenon created on the moon by lunar craters, see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_x" title="Lunar x">
        Lunar x
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em">
       <tr>
        <th class="summary" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: #eedd82;">
         Google Lunar XPRIZE
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GoogleLunarXPRIZE_Logo.png" title="Google Lunar X Prize logo">
          <img alt="Google Lunar X Prize logo" data-file-height="179" data-file-width="556" height="71" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/GoogleLunarXPRIZE_Logo.png/220px-GoogleLunarXPRIZE_Logo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/GoogleLunarXPRIZE_Logo.png/330px-GoogleLunarXPRIZE_Logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/GoogleLunarXPRIZE_Logo.png/440px-GoogleLunarXPRIZE_Logo.png 2x" width="220"/>
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">
         Awarded for
        </th>
        <td>
         "landing a robot on the surface of the Moon, traveling 500 meters over the lunar surface, and sending images and data back to the Earth."
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLXPabout2009_1-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-GLXPabout2009-1">
           [1]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">
         Country
        </th>
        <td class="location">
         Worldwide
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">
         Presented by
        </th>
        <td class="attendee">
         <a href="/wiki/X_Prize_Foundation" title="X Prize Foundation">
          X Prize Foundation
         </a>
         (organizer),
         <br/>
         <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
          Google
         </a>
         (sponsor)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">
         Reward(s)
        </th>
        <td>
         US$20 million for the winner,
         <br/>
         US$5 million for second place,
         <br/>
         US$4 million in technical bonuses,
         <br/>
         US$1 million diversity award
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">
         Website
        </th>
        <td>
         <a class="external text" href="http://lunar.xprize.org/" rel="nofollow">
          lunar.xprize.org
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>

         Trailer for the prize.

      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Google Lunar XPRIZE
       </b>
       (
       <b>
        GLXP
       </b>
       ), sometimes referred to as
       <b>
        Moon 2.0
       </b>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koman_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Koman-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was a 2007–2018
       <a href="/wiki/Inducement_prize_contest" title="Inducement prize contest">
        inducement prize
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Space_competition" title="Space competition">
        space competition
       </a>
       organized by the
       <a href="/wiki/X_Prize_Foundation" title="X Prize Foundation">
        X Prize Foundation
       </a>
       , and sponsored by
       <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
        Google
       </a>
       . The challenge called for
       <a href="/wiki/Private_spaceflight" title="Private spaceflight">
        privately-funded
       </a>
       teams to be the first to land a robotic spacecraft on
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        the Moon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_rover" title="Lunar rover">
        travel
       </a>
       500 meters, and transmit back to Earth high-definition video and images.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The prize ended in early 2018 when no team was able to schedule, confirm and pay for a launch attempt.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2015,
       <a href="/wiki/X_Prize_Foundation" title="X Prize Foundation">
        XPRIZE
       </a>
       announced that the competition deadline would be extended to December 2017 if at least one team could secure a verified launch contract by 31 December 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two teams secured such a launch contract, and the deadline was extended.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In August 2017, the deadline was extended again, to 31 March 2018.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2018-ext_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-2018-ext-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Entering 2018, five teams remained officially in the competition, but the signs were that it was unlikely anyone would be able to make the deadline of 31 March 2018.
       <a href="/wiki/SpaceIL" title="SpaceIL">
        SpaceIL
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Moon_Express" title="Moon Express">
        Moon Express
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Synergy_Moon" title="Synergy Moon">
        Synergy Moon
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_Indus" title="Team Indus">
        Team Indus
       </a>
       , and Team
       <a href="/wiki/Hakuto" title="Hakuto">
        Hakuto
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       having secured verified launch contracts (with
       <a href="/wiki/Spaceflight_Industries" title="Spaceflight Industries">
        Spaceflight Industries
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_Lab" title="Rocket Lab">
        Rocket Lab
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Interorbital_Systems" title="Interorbital Systems">
        Interorbital Systems
       </a>
       , and a joint
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISRO" title="ISRO">
        ISRO
       </a>
       launch for the latter two teams).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:3-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-synergylaunchres_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-synergylaunchres-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 23 January 2018, the X Prize Foundation announced that "no team would be able to make a launch attempt to reach the Moon by the [31 March 2018] deadline... and the US$30 million Google Lunar XPRIZE will go unclaimed."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20170123_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sn20170123-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

          <span class="tocnumber">

          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Terrestrial Milestone Prizes
          </span>
         </a>
         <ul>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">
           <a href="#Overview_2">
            <span class="tocnumber">
             5.1
            </span>

             Overview
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11">
           <a href="#Selected_teams">
            <span class="tocnumber">
             5.2
            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             Selected teams
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12">
         <a href="#Confirmed_launch_reservations_by_the_end_of_2016">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           6
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Confirmed launch reservations by the end of 2016
          </span>
         </a>
         <ul>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">
           <a href="#Others">
            <span class="tocnumber">
             6.1
            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             Others
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14">
         <a href="#See_also">

          </span>

          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15">
         <a href="#References">

          </span>

        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16">

          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Competition_summary">
        Competition summary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Competition summary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The Google Lunar XPRIZE was announced at the
       <a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)#NextFest" title="Wired (magazine)">
        Wired Nextfest
       </a>
       on 13 September 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The competition offers a total of US$30 million in prizes to the first privately funded teams to land a robot on the Moon that successfully travels more than 500 meters (1,640 ft) and transmits back high-definition images and video. The first team to do so will claim the US$20 million grand prize; while the second team to accomplish the same tasks will earn a US$5 million second prize.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Teams can also earn additional money by completing additional tasks beyond the baseline requirements required to win the grand or second prize, such as traveling ten times the baseline requirements (greater than 5,000 meters (3 mi)), capturing images of the remains of
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">
        Apollo program
       </a>
       hardware or other man-made objects on the Moon, verifying from the lunar surface the recent detection of water ice on the Moon, or surviving a lunar night. Additionally, a US$1 million diversity award may be given to teams that make significant strides in promoting ethnic diversity in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/STEM_fields" title="STEM fields">
        STEM fields
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       To provide an added incentive for teams to complete their missions quickly, it was announced that the prize would decrease from US$20 million to US$15 million whenever a government-led mission lands on and explores the lunar surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLXPabout2009_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-GLXPabout2009-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Chinese
       <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_3" title="Chang'e 3">
        Chang'e 3
       </a>
       probe landed on the Moon in December 2013, however, in November 2013, as the launch of the probe approached, it was agreed between the organizers and the teams to drop this rule.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2015,
       <a href="/wiki/X_Prize_Foundation" title="X Prize Foundation">
        XPRIZE
       </a>
       announced that the competition deadline would be extended to December 2017 if at least one team could secure a verified launch contract by 31 December 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two teams secured such a launch contract, and the deadline was extended.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_6-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       XPRIZE announced 5 finalists on 24 January 2017.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finalists_2017_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Finalists_2017-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/SpaceIL" title="SpaceIL">
        SpaceIL
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Moon_Express" title="Moon Express">
        Moon Express
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Synergy_Moon" title="Synergy Moon">
        Synergy Moon
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_Indus" title="Team Indus">
        Team Indus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hakuto" title="Hakuto">
        Hakuto
       </a>
       having secured verified launch contracts for 2017 (with
       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">
        SpaceX
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_Lab" title="Rocket Lab">
        Rocket Lab
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Interorbital_Systems" title="Interorbital Systems">
        Interorbital Systems
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isro" title="Isro">
        ISRO
       </a>
       respectively).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_6-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:3-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-synergylaunchres_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-synergylaunchres-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       All other teams had until the end of 2016 to secure a verified launch contract, but failed to meet this deadline and are no longer in the competition.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:4-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Google Lunar XPRIZE expires when all constituent purses have been claimed, or on 31 March 2018. Another extension of the deadline has been ruled out by Google
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , even though none of the four final teams were able to launch their vehicles by the end of March. As of such, the prize went unclaimed, as stated by
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Diamandis" title="Peter Diamandis">
        Peter Diamandis
       </a>
       , X Prize founder and chairman.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">
        Overview
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Overview">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Diamandis" title="Peter Diamandis">
        Peter Diamandis
       </a>
       , the project founder, wrote on the official web page in 2007:
      </p>
      <table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
       <tr>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">
         “
        </td>
        <td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">
         It has been many decades since we explored the Moon from the lunar surface, and it could be another 6–8 years before any government returns. Even then, it will be at a large expense, and probably with little public involvement.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
          <a href="#cite_note-22">
           [22]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">
         ”
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The goal of the Google Lunar X Prize is similar to that of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ansari_X_Prize" title="Ansari X Prize">
        Ansari X Prize
       </a>
       : to inspire a new generation of private investment in hopes of developing more cost-effective technologies and materials to overcome many limitations of space exploration that are currently taken for granted.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The Google Lunar XPRIZE was announced in 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ieee20140605_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ieee20140605-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_of_the_prize">
        Origin of the prize
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Origin of the prize">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carnegie_Mellon_University_Google_Lunar_X-Prize_Moon_Rover.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Carnegie_Mellon_University_Google_Lunar_X-Prize_Moon_Rover.jpg/250px-Carnegie_Mellon_University_Google_Lunar_X-Prize_Moon_Rover.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Carnegie_Mellon_University_Google_Lunar_X-Prize_Moon_Rover.jpg/375px-Carnegie_Mellon_University_Google_Lunar_X-Prize_Moon_Rover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Carnegie_Mellon_University_Google_Lunar_X-Prize_Moon_Rover.jpg/500px-Carnegie_Mellon_University_Google_Lunar_X-Prize_Moon_Rover.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carnegie_Mellon_University_Google_Lunar_X-Prize_Moon_Rover.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">
          Carnegie Mellon University
         </a>
         lunar rover
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Similar to the way in which the
       <a href="/wiki/Ansari_X_Prize" title="Ansari X Prize">
        Ansari XPRIZE
       </a>
       was formed, the Google Lunar XPRIZE was created out of a former venture of Peter Diamandis to achieve a similar goal. Dr Diamandis served as CEO of
       <a href="/wiki/BlastOff!_Corporation" title="BlastOff! Corporation">
        BlastOff! Corporation
       </a>
       , a commercial initiative to land a robotic spacecraft on the Moon as a mix of entertainment, internet, and space. Although it was ultimately unsuccessful, the BlastOff! initiative paved the way for the Google Lunar X Prize.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Initially,
       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
        NASA
       </a>
       was the planned sponsor and the prize purse was just US$20 million. As NASA is a federal agency of the United States government, and thus funded by US tax money, the prize would only have been available to teams from the United States. The original intention was to propose the idea to other national space agencies, including the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">
        European Space Agency
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">
        Japanese space agency
       </a>
       , in the hope that they would offer similar prize purses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thelaunchpad.xprize_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-thelaunchpad.xprize-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       However, budget setbacks stopped NASA from sponsoring the prize. Peter Diamandis then presented the idea to
       <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">
        Larry Page
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin" title="Sergey Brin">
        Sergey Brin
       </a>
       , co-founders of Google, at an
       <a href="/wiki/X_Prize_Foundation" title="X Prize Foundation">
        XPRIZE
       </a>
       fundraiser. They agreed to sponsor it, and also to increase the prize purse to US$30 million, allowing for a second place prize, as well as bonus prizes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thelaunchpad.xprize_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-thelaunchpad.xprize-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2014)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Extensions_of_the_deadline">
        Extensions of the deadline
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Extensions of the deadline">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The prize was originally announced in 2007 as "a contest to put a robotic rover on the Moon by 2012,"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koman_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Koman-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with a $20 million prize to the winner if the landing was achieved by 2012; the prize decreased to $15M until the end of 2014, at which point the contest would conclude. The five-year deadline was optimistic about schedule, and Jeff Foust commented in
       <i>
        Space Review
       </i>
       that as the end of 2012 approached, "no team appeared that close to mounting a reasonable bid to win it."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2010, the deadline was extended by one year, with the prize to expire at the end of December 2015, and the reduction of the grand prize from $20 million to $15 million changed from originally 2012 to "if a government mission successfully lands on the lunar surface."
      </p>
      <p>
       On 16 December 2014, XPRIZE announced another extension in the prize deadline from 31 December 2015 to 31 December 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extended2016_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-extended2016-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In May 2015, the foundation announced another extension of the deadline. The deadline for winning the prize was now December 2017, but contingent on at least one team showing by 31 December 2015 that they have a secured contract for launch. On 9 October 2015, team
       <a href="/wiki/SpaceIL" title="SpaceIL">
        SpaceIL
       </a>
       announced their officially-verified launch contract with
       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">
        SpaceX
       </a>
       , therefore extending the competition until the end of 2017.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_6-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 16 August 2017, the deadline was extended again, to 31 March 2018.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2018-ext_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-2018-ext-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The latest reports are, as of 22 January 2018 is that none of the remaining teams will be able to claim the Google X-Prize money due to the inability to launch before the final deadline.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Objections_to_the_Heritage_Bonus_Prizes">
        Objections to the Heritage Bonus Prizes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Objections to the Heritage Bonus Prizes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Some observers have raised objections to the inclusion of the two "Heritage Bonus Prizes," particularly the Apollo Heritage Bonus Prize, which will award an additional estimated US$1 million to the first group that successfully delivers images and videos of the landing site of one of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo_Program" title="Apollo Program">
        Apollo Program
       </a>
       landing sites, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Tranquility_Base" title="Tranquility Base">
        Tranquility Base
       </a>
       , after landing on the lunar surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAT_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LAT-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Such sites are widely regarded as archaeologically and culturally significant, and some have expressed concern that a team attempting to win this heritage bonus might inadvertently damage or destroy such a site, either during the landing phase of the mission, or by piloting a rover around the site.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SEED_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SEED-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a result, some archaeologists are on record calling for the Foundation to cancel the heritage bonus and to ban groups from targeting landing zones within 100 kilometers (62 mi) of previous sites.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HD-Video_Interview_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HD-Video_Interview-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In turn, the Foundation has noted that, as part of the competition's educational goals, it hopes these bonuses will foster debate about how to respectfully visit previous lunar landing sites, but that it does not see itself as the appropriate adjudicator of such an internationally relevant and interdisciplinary issue. This response left detractors unsatisfied.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SciAm2_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SciAm2-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Foundation points to the historical precedent set by the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_12" title="Apollo 12">
        Apollo 12
       </a>
       mission, which landed nearby the previous
       <a href="/wiki/Surveyor_3" title="Surveyor 3">
        Surveyor 3
       </a>
       robotic probe.
       <a href="/wiki/Pete_Conrad" title="Pete Conrad">
        Pete Conrad
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Bean" title="Alan Bean">
        Alan Bean
       </a>
       approached and inspected Surveyor 3 and even removed some parts from it to be returned to Earth for study; new scientific results from that heritage visit, on the exposure of manmade objects to conditions in outer space, were still being published in leading papers nearly four decades later.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASASurv_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASASurv-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, as Surveyor 3 and Apollo 12 were both NASA missions, there was no controversy at the time.
      </p>
      <p>
       In January 2011, NASA's Manager for Lunar Commercial Space noted on Twitter that work was underway to provide insight and guidelines on how lunar heritage sites could be protected while still allowing visitations that will yield critical science.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Twitter_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Twitter-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       And in July 2011, NASA issued
       <i>
        Recommendations to Space-Faring Entities: How to Protect and Preserve the Historic and Scientific Value of U.S. Government Lunar Artifacts
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These guidelines were developed with the assistance of Dr. Beth O'Leary, an anthropology professor at New Mexico State University in Las Cruces, and a recognized leader in the emerging field of
       <a href="/wiki/Space_archaeology" title="Space archaeology">
        space archaeology
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.com_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-space.com-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, these are only guidelines and recommendations and are not enforceable beyond the possibility of "moral sanctions."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Times_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-New_York_Times-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An organization called For All Moonkind is now working to develop an international treaty that will include enforceable provisions designed to manage access to the Apollo sites and protect and preserve those sites, as well as others on the Moon, as the common heritage of all humankind.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-For_All_Moonkind_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-For_All_Moonkind-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nevertheless, some of the Apollo astronauts themselves have expressed support for the bonus, with
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">
        Apollo 11
       </a>
       moonwalker
       <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin" title="Buzz Aldrin">
        Buzz Aldrin
       </a>
       appearing at the Google Lunar XPRIZE's initial announcement and reading a plaque signed by the majority of his fellow surviving Apollo Astronauts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aldrin_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Aldrin-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prize_not_won">
        Prize not won
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Prize not won">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On 23 January 2018, the X Prize Foundation announced that "no team would be able to make a launch attempt to reach the Moon by the [31 March 2018] deadline... and the
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        US$30 million
       </span>
       Google Lunar XPRIZE will go unclaimed."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20170123_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-sn20170123-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Competitors">
        Competitors
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Competitors">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Registration in the Google Lunar X Prize closed as of 31 December 2010. The complete roster of teams
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="This term requires quantification. (January 2018)">
           quantify
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       was announced in February 2011. As of January 2017, there were just five officially registered Google Lunar X Prize teams continuing to pursue the prize objectives, as other teams had left the competition entirely, failed to achieve a competition interim
       <a href="/wiki/Milestone_(project_management)" title="Milestone (project management)">
        milestone
       </a>
       , or merged with other teams:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Initially 32 teams were registered, with 16 teams having actively participated in all activities and only 5 teams satisfying the rule requiring a verified launch contract by 31 December 2016.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>

         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terrestrial_Milestone_Prizes">
        Terrestrial Milestone Prizes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Terrestrial Milestone Prizes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview_2">
        Overview
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Overview">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In November 2013 the X-Prize organization announced that several milestone prizes will be awarded to teams for demonstrating key technologies prior to the actual mission. A total of
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        US$6 million
       </span>
       could be awarded throughout 2014 for achieving the following milestones:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milestone_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-milestone-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        $1 million (for up to 3 teams) for the
        <i>
         Lander System Milestone Prize
        </i>
        to demonstrate hardware and software that enables a soft-landing on the moon.
       </li>
       <li>
        $500,000 (for up to 4 teams) for the
        <i>
         Mobility Subsystem Milestone Prize
        </i>
        to demonstrate a mobility system that allows the craft to move 500 meters after landing.
       </li>
       <li>
        $250,000 (for up to 4 teams) for the
        <i>
         Imaging Subsystem Milestone Prize
        </i>
        for producing "Mooncasts" consisting of high-quality images and video on the lunar surface.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_teams">
        Selected teams
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Lunar_X_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Selected teams">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In February 2014, a judging panel selected five teams which could compete for several interim prizes based on their proposals to achieve particular goals. The teams and their ultimate awards were:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

         ($250,000)

        </th>

      <p>
       The five selected teams were required to accomplish the milestones outlined in their submissions through testing and mission simulations, in order to be awarded the interim prizes. The teams had until October 2014 to complete the prize requirements. The winners were officially awarded on 26 January 2015 in San Francisco.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extended2016_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-extended2016-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

        <td>
         Was to have been a piggyback on
         <a href="/wiki/TeamIndus" title="TeamIndus">
          TeamIndus
         </a>
         's
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PSLV" title="PSLV">
          PSLV
         </a>
         flight.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indus-hakuto_44-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-indus-hakuto-44">
           [44]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Contract for launch vehicle was cancelled in early 2018.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inc42-20180109_108-2">
          <a href="#cite_note-inc42-20180109-108">
           [108]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20170123_12-5">
          <a href="#cite_note-sn20170123-12">
           [12]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>

      <p>
       Another seven of the competitors who were unable to get a verified launch contract by 31 December 2016, leading their disqualification from Google Lunar X Prize, are however planning to launch their crafts independently, though not in competition but for research and commercial purposes.

         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation news">
           Foust, Jeff (2018-01-23).
           <a class="external text" href="http://spacenews.com/google-lunar-x-prize-to-end-without-winner/" rel="nofollow">
            "Google Lunar X Prize to end without winner"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/SpaceNews" title="SpaceNews">
             SpaceNews
            </a>
           </i>
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             2018-01-24
            </span>
           </span>
           .
           <q>
            The foundation running the Google Lunar X Prize announced Jan. 23 that the $20 million grand prize for a commercial lunar lander will expire at the end of March without a winner. The X Prize Foundation said none of its five finalist teams would be able to launch a mission before the current deadline of March 31. That deadline has been extended several times in the past, but foundation officials previously said there would be no further extensions of the competition.
           </q>
          </cite>

        <li id="cite_note-glxp20150223-53">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-glxp20150223_53-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation web">
           <a class="external text" href="http://lunar.xprize.org/press-release/two-google-lunar-xprize-teams-announce-rideshare-partnership-mission-moon-2016" rel="nofollow">
            "Two Google Lunar XPRIZE Teams Announce Rideshare Partnership For Mission to the Moon in 2016"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            xprize.org
           </i>
           . Xprize Foundation. 23 February 2015
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             6 March
            </span>
            2015
           </span>
           .
           <q>
            <i>
             Hakuto [... and fellow competitor] Astrobotic [will] carry a pair of rovers to the moon. Astrobotic plans to launch its Google Lunar XPRIZE mission on a SpaceX Falcon 9 rocket from Cape Canaveral, Fla., during the second half of 2016. HAKUTO's twin rovers, Moonraker and Tetris, will piggyback on Astrobotic's Griffin lander to reach the lunar surface. Upon touchdown, the rovers will be released simultaneously ... in pursuit of the $20M Google Lunar XPRIZE Grand Prize.
            </i>
           </q>
          </cite>
